# About Me

Amanda King is a part-time Master of Public Management candidate at Carnegie Mellon University Heinz College of Information Systems and Public Policy. Her preferred pronouns are she, her, and hers. For the last seven years, she's worked full-time in public relations and journalism. 

# What I Hope To Learn

As a communications professional, Amanda is hoping to supplement her writing with effective data visualizations. After she graduates in May 2020, Amanda hopes to become a Director of Communications and/or Content Strategy for a nonprofit or governmental organization.

## Assignment 2

###### General Government Debt Visualization - Bar Chart

###### General Government Debt Visualization - Beeswarm Plot

Below is a beeswarm plot that represents government debt by country from 1995 - 2018. I created it using the online tool RAWGraphs. The data is from The Organization for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD). To interpret this data, we know that the larger the circle, the larger the debt a country holds.

###### Five Countries with the Highest Government Debt From 1995-2018 - Area Graph

Below is an area graph that represents government debt by country from 1995 - 2018. I created it using RAWGraphs and the same data utilized in the previous visualization. I incorporated a red color palette from ColorBrewer and applied it to the top five countries with the most government debt. 

I chose an area graph to represent the data set since it sits in a time series. This is my first experience working with an area graph, and I think it's an interesting way to visualize data by comparing it.

###### Compare and Contrast

The visualizations represented in the above beeswarm and area graph are very different. I find that the data in the beeswarm plot is more effectively visualized. The viewer can easily see the countries with the largest vs. smallest debt just by simply looking at the size of the dots. The area graph is not as clear. For instance, it brings in a color palette, while the beeswarm plot did not. It's also a little more difficult to point out the countries with the largest debt. Yet, it was really interesting to see the same data represented in two different ways. I'm overall happy I had the opportunity to experiment with both types of these visualization methods.

*Source: oecd.org*

## Assignment 3 

I chose to critique and redesign the bar chart titled "A Gilded Age" at the bottom of [this Bloomberg article.](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2019-09-13/big-reads-on-economics-negative-rates-u-s-factories-shake) After reviewing the visualization, I wanted to improve its title, color scheme and data organization. Also, I had never worked with data from the World Wealth and Income Database (WID), so that interested me.

Next, I critiqued the graphic focusing on what worked, and didn't work so well. I touched on the confusion the title caused since the Gilded Age was the time between the Civil War and WWI, but the data was from 1980 and 2010. In addition, I appreciated that the designer followed Bloomberg's style guide, but I thought a green color scheme could be more effective since the data represents a financial element - the share of pre-tax income that goes to the top 1%.

After the critique, I sketched two variations (pictured below) of the redesigned bar chart by making one vertical, and one horizontal, but with a different color scheme, title, description and some other minor variations.

![Sketch 1](/images/IMG-9693.jpg)
Format: ![bar chart sketch](url)

![Sketch 2](/images/IMG-9692.jpg)
Format: ![bar chart sketch 2](url)

I presented the wireframes to two potential users. One user said he thought the vertical bar chart was more effective. In addition, the other user recommended listing the countries by height. I then integrated their feedback into a second round of redesign by transforming the horizontal bars into a vertical orientation, and ordering the countries by ascending height instead of by alphabetical listing. This created a more dramatic effect of the increase in share of pre-tax income.

My redesigned data visualization (pictured below) was created using Infogram. In it, I show that from 1980-2010, the share of pre-tax income that went to the top 1% of earners dramatically increased worldwide. 

<div class="infogram-embed" data-id="85ff39e6-61ec-4c69-8656-0f5b5435f36d" data-type="interactive" data-title="Bar Chart"></div><script>!function(e,t,s,i){var n="InfogramEmbeds",o=e.getElementsByTagName("script")[0],d=/^http:/.test(e.location)?"http:":"https:";if(/^\/{2}/.test(i)&&(i=d+i),window[n]&&window[n].initialized)window[n].process&&window[n].process();else if(!e.getElementById(s)){var r=e.createElement("script");r.async=1,r.id=s,r.src=i,o.parentNode.insertBefore(r,o)}}(document,0,"infogram-async","https://e.infogram.com/js/dist/embed-loader-min.js");</script><div style="padding:8px 0;font-family:Arial!important;font-size:13px!important;line-height:15px!important;text-align:center;border-top:1px solid #dadada;margin:0 30px"><a href="https://infogram.com/85ff39e6-61ec-4c69-8656-0f5b5435f36d" style="color:#989898!important;text-decoration:none!important;" target="_blank">Bar Chart</a><br><a href="https://infogram.com" style="color:#989898!important;text-decoration:none!important;" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">Infogram</a></div>

This chart provides a more interactive way to represent the data by allowing the user to toggle between the 1980 and 2010 data. This eliminates the confusion the hover tool on the Bloomberg visualization caused. I didn't even realize it was a feature until I sat with the chart for a few minutes. I also felt there wasn't a need for a key with this new experience. In addition, I decided to include Italy, another major economy that I thought shouldn't be negated. I attempted to include Brazil as well, but the 1980 data was not available. The data is represented by only green bars. I attempted to display a different title that readers could easily tie to the chart. I left off the note since it doesn't make sense without the associated copy. Overall, I think it provides a more interactive experience for the user and shows the increase in income more dramatically.
